< Review>
We were about to leave Half Moon Bay after lunch when my wife spotted the gelato joint in this side street. I believe we met Gulino, a young man from Italy. He described how he made his gelato, not ice-cream. Unlike ice-cream, gelato contains no air and therefore is much smoother and richer.
Indeed we loved his gelato- I forgot what flavours. We sat leisurely on the pavement and enjoyed it in the sunshine.
At the end we suggested to Gelino that he should place his advertisement sign board at the main street to boost sales instead of putting the gelato to waste.< /Review>

< Text>
AH, yeah! White Dragon. I really wish I could just download my experience into you because there is so *much* but that wouldn‚Äôt work so now I‚Äôm scrambling around for words to publicly describe my experience here.

Martial arts are inherently difficult so if you are looking for an easy quick kind of workout experience I don‚Äôt recommend it. But if you are looking for an active lifestyle option and aren‚Äôt afraid of things like discipline, hard work, or being challenged, and you don‚Äôt mind learning in an all-ages environment, then come here.

If I had to base my recommendation off of the first three weeks of training I would have told you I had made a mistake. I was kind of freaked out and confused. That says something about what I was like back then. The thing is learning takes time. Even though it was hard for me I stuck it out, and man, I‚Äôm glad I did!

I‚Äôve been training consistently at the La Mesa school for about 4 ¬Ω years. They emphasis self-defence and health (both really awesome things) through traditional Chinese martial arts. The staff is held to a high standard and they are willing to workout any issues you may have with them or the training process. I have found the them to be consistently dedicated, generous and respectful.

As with any new environment expect to be a little confused at first. You will be paired with a privet instructor and you can ask them all the questions you have no matter how lame.

For me just access to this awesome community is worth the time and expense and I‚Äôm definitely stronger and more confident than I was when I began training and, to me, that is amazing.

So seriously try it. Sticking around was/is the *best mistake* I continue to make.<//Text>

<rate>5< /rate>< text>
This school is great, there's a strong sense of community and camaraderie among the students. We're always looking to support one another, and we understand that in building  each other up we ultimately create better martial artists in the long run.

The instructors are dedicated and clearly passionate about the job they do; when they're not teaching their students or running classes, they're always helping students with questions.

We get to learn traditional Choy Li Fut hand and weapons forms, kickboxing, Yang-style Tai Chi Chuan, and grappling, to name a few. Anyone who comes with an earnest interest and dedication to the art form will be greatly rewarded.

And if that doesn't pique your interest, consider this quote from Bruce Lee: "Choy Li Fut is the most effective system that I've seen for fighting more than one person," "[It] is one of the most difficult styles to attack and defend against. Choy Li Fut is the only style [of kung fu] that traveled to Thailand to fight the Thai boxers and hadn't lost."< /text>

<name>Morgan A.< /name><time>1475295535543< /time><rate>5< /rate><Review>Where to start. First off let me state that I wish I could give the school 11 stars!

I joined White Dragon school in May 2016 at the referral of my spiritual counselor, as a way to find balance and give myself a healthy outlet to channel some intense internal energy. As I have tried everything from home workout dvds, 30 day internet challenges and a couple big name gyms I was skeptical about how interested they could keep me since I tend to lose motivation and self accountability when it comes to working out. Still I  signed up for the 2 part introductory lessons with an open mind. After my first lesson I was hooked. After my second I decided that White Dragon was exactly what I needed in my life and committed to a one year second tier membership. I use the word committed here because while its not cheap the membership is worth every penny. The knowledge they teach and the offered resources( for example: video training for at home study, seminars, etc)  are a complete investment in yourself and your journey. I cant say this enough, you get back what you put into this. Take advantage of what the school offers and its more than worth the price. They didn't try to oversell me on the packages and really worked with me to determine what the best level of commitment would work in conjuncture with my own personal goals. With my membership I have access to a multitude of group classes that are offered both in the early afternoons and on alternate days in the evenings and one 30 min personal lesson each week (special shout out to Mr. Cuiriz you're awesome!).

The Chief Instructor Tai Sifu Tittle is always approachable and friendly and every instructor I have taken classes with are A+. They are patient, encouraging and just as dedicated to their students success as the students themselves. One of my main concerns prior to joining was that there might be a "macho" vibe in the martial arts community. SO NOT THE CASE. Everyone I have come into contact with at White Dragon starting from day one has treated me with the utmost friendliness, professionalism and respect. This statement goes for the other students as well! This school truly radiates a family like energy.

I started out this journey for myself but can honestly that after just 4 months I feel like I am a part of something bigger than myself. <rate>5</rate><text>I am 54 years old and became a student at White dragon about 9 months ago. I say my age only to encourage my peers to not let the age of your body hold you back. It seems that once I hit 53 I began to feel achey and more tired. Never being one to sleep in I was having a harder time wanting to get out of bed. My mood was becoming "Ho Hum" which I never though was possible. A friend (who is also an instructor at WD) inspired me when I heard him speak on his experience as a martial artist of Choy li Fut. I was in awe. My world immediatley opened up as if a gift, a way out of my "physical stuckness," landed on my lap.

The next day I walked into White Dragon Martial Arts School in La Mesa and I don't see myself ever leaving.  In the group classes I am usually surrounded by students much younger than me but I want to assure you this does not matter. We are all treated with the same respect and kindness. I will say, we are all expected to do the best we can and to push ourselves, but this is the way, the discipline of being a martial artist. I love the challenge on so many levels, even on the days I feel so defeated by the pace of my learning, my flexibility or strength. My instructor reminds me that we are all learning all the time no matter what sash level we are at.  I hold onto this.

Having unlimited group classes supports the individual training I get with my instructor weekly. The classes that focus more on physical fitness to strengthen and develop endurance are intense. I sweat in 10 minutes in these workouts what it used to take in a 50-minute cycling class. Plus, I use my whole body now, every inch of it in ways I never have. I love that my brain is being stimulated and forced to rewire itself which is good brain health, helps prevent neurological problems that come with age.

I could go on and on singing praises from the exceptional staff lead by Tai Sifu Donald Tittle to the quality of program, but I especially want to speak to the older crowd. Don't hesitate, don't let fear block you. White Dragon is a supportive and exciting place to learn, grow, be challenged and stay healthy. I thank everyone at White Dragon and hope to give back in some way what they have given me.</text>< pictures>

After a car accident, I went to Cypress Urgent Care. When I checked in I was told there were only 2 patients ahead of me. Even though, I told them I was in a car accident, was limping and had a clearly broken finger, I waited over 2 hours in a hospital gown in a cold room while the female PA continued to take COVID related patients ahead of me. I could hear all of the visits as they were on speaker. Some people wanted COVID clearances for work while others wanted prescriptions for coughs. Yet, I sat shivering in pain. Even though I heard the medical assistant kindly remind her a car accident patient was in a room, she kept taking COVID related patients ahead of me. Ultimately, I got dressed and spoke with the receptionist to let her know I had not been seen. The receptionist stated that the PA had patients outside in an alley to see first.
